<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interlacing_dialogues">Interlacing dialogues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Interlacing dialogues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Literary scholar M. Keith Booker argues that Vargas Llosa perfects the technique of interlacing dialogues in his novel <i>The Green House</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Booker33_48-4"><a href="#cite_note-Booker33-48">[48]</a></sup> By combining two conversations that occur at different times, he creates the illusion of a <a href="/wiki/Flashback_(narrative)" title="Flashback (narrative)">flashback</a>. Vargas Llosa also sometimes uses this technique as a means of shifting location by weaving together two concurrent conversations happening in different places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Booker14_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Booker14-117">[117]</a></sup> This technique is a staple of his repertoire, which he began using near the end of his first novel, <i>The Time of the Hero</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> However, he does not use interlacing dialogues in the same way in all of his novels. For example, in <i>The Green House</i> the technique is used in a serious fashion to achieve a sober tone and to focus on the interrelatedness of important events separated in time or space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In contrast, <i>Captain Pantoja and the Special Service</i> employs this strategy for comic effects and uses simpler spatial shifts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> This device is similar to both <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Woolf" title="Virginia Woolf">Virginia Woolf</a>'s mixing of different characters' soliloquies and Gustave Flaubert's <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">counterpoint</a> technique in which he blends together conversation with other events, such as speeches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Booker14_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Booker14-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_influences">Literary influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Literary influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vargas Llosa's first literary influences were relatively obscure Peruvian writers such as <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Ad%C3%A1n" title="Martín Adán">Martín Adán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Oquendo_de_Amat" title="Carlos Oquendo de Amat">Carlos Oquendo de Amat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Moro" title="César Moro">César Moro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro3_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Castro3-121">[121]</a></sup> As a young writer, he looked to these revolutionary novelists in search of new narrative structures and techniques in order to delineate a more contemporary, multifaceted experience of urban Peru. He was looking for a style different from the traditional descriptions of land and rural life made famous by Peru's foremost novelist at the time, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Arguedas" title="José María Arguedas">José María Arguedas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Vargas Llosa wrote of Arguedas's work that it was "an example of old-fashioned regionalism that had already exhausted its imaginary possibilities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro3_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Castro3-121">[121]</a></sup> Although he did not share Arguedas's passion for indigenous reality, Vargas Llosa admired and respected the novelist for his contributions to Peruvian literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Indeed, he has published a book-length study on his work, <i>La utopía arcaica</i> (1996).</p>
<p>Rather than restrict himself to Peruvian literature, Vargas Llosa also looked abroad for literary inspiration. Two French figures, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Existentialist" title="Existentialist">existentialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a> and novelist <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Flaubert" title="Gustave Flaubert">Gustave Flaubert</a>, influenced both his technique and style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Sartre's influence is most prevalent in Vargas Llosa's extensive use of conversation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro6_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Castro6-125">[125]</a></sup> The epigraph of <i>The Time of the Hero</i>, his first novel, is also taken directly from Sartre's work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Flaubert's artistic independence—his novels' disregard of reality and morals—has always been admired by Vargas Llosa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> who wrote a book-length study of Flaubert's <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics" title="Aesthetics">aesthetics</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Perpetual_Orgy" title="The Perpetual Orgy">The Perpetual Orgy</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In his analysis of Flaubert, Vargas Llosa questions the revolutionary power of literature in a political setting; this is in contrast to his earlier view that "literature is an act of rebellion", thus marking a transition in Vargas Llosa's aesthetic beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kristal81_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kristal81-129">[129]</a></sup> Other critics such as Sabine Köllmann argue that his belief in the transforming power of literature is one of the great continuities that characterize his fictional and non-fictional work, and link his early statement that 'Literature is Fire' with his Nobel Prize Speech 'In Praise of Reading and Writing'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of Vargas Llosa's favourite novelists, and arguably the most influential on his writing career, is the American <a href="/wiki/William_Faulkner" title="William Faulkner">William Faulkner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Vargas Llosa considers Faulkner "the writer who perfected the methods of the modern novel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kristal26_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kristal26-132">[132]</a></sup> Both writers' styles include intricate changes in time and narration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro6_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Castro6-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kristal26_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kristal26-132">[132]</a></sup> In <i>The Time of the Hero</i>, for example, aspects of Vargas Llosa's plot, his main character's development and his use of narrative time are influenced by his favourite Faulkner novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Light_in_August" title="Light in August">Light in August</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the studies of Arguedas and Flaubert, Vargas Llosa has written literary criticisms of other authors that he has admired, such as Gabriel García Márquez, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro116_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Castro116-134">[134]</a></sup> The main goals of his non-fiction works are to acknowledge the influence of these authors on his writing, and to recognize a connection between himself and the other writers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro116_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Castro116-134">[134]</a></sup> critic Sara Castro-Klarén argues that he offers little systematic analysis of these authors' literary techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro116_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-Castro116-134">[134]</a></sup> In <i>The Perpetual Orgy</i>, for example, he discusses the relationship between his own aesthetics and Flaubert's, rather than focusing on Flaubert's alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mario Vargas Llosa is considered a major Latin American writer, alongside other authors such as <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">Octavio Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Cort%C3%A1zar" title="Julio Cortázar">Julio Cortázar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">Carlos Fuentes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro1_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Castro1-136">[136]</a></sup> In his book <i>The New Novel in Latin America</i> (<i>La Nueva Novela</i>), Fuentes offers an in-depth literary criticism of the positive influence Vargas Llosa's work has had on Latin American literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lamb102_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lamb102-137">[137]</a></sup> Indeed, for the literary critic <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Martin" title="Gerald Martin">Gerald Martin</a>, writing in 1987, Vargas Llosa was "perhaps the most successful ... certainly the most controversial Latin American novelist of the past twenty-five years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of Vargas Llosa's narratives have been translated into multiple languages, marking his international critical success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castro1_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Castro1-136">[136]</a></sup> Vargas Llosa is also noted for his substantial contribution to journalism, an accomplishment characteristic of few other Latin American writers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> He is recognized among those who have most consciously promoted literature in general, and more specifically the novel itself, as avenues for meaningful commentary about life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> During his career, he has written more than a dozen novels and many other books and stories, and, for decades, he has been a voice for Latin American literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> He has won numerous awards for his writing, from the 1959 <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Premio_Leopoldo_Alas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Premio Leopoldo Alas (page does not exist)">Premio Leopoldo Alas</a></i> and the 1962 <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Premio_Biblioteca_Breve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Premio Biblioteca Breve (page does not exist)">Premio Biblioteca Breve</a></i> to the 1993 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premio_Planeta" title="Premio Planeta">Premio Planeta</a></i> (for <i>Death in the Andes</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Prize" title="Jerusalem Prize">Jerusalem Prize</a> in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The literary critic <a href="/wiki/Harold_Bloom" title="Harold Bloom">Harold Bloom</a> has included his novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_War_of_the_End_of_the_World" title="The War of the End of the World">The War of the End of the World</a></i> in his list of essential literary works in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Canon" title="Western Canon">Western Canon</a>. An important distinction he has received is the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize" title="Miguel de Cervantes Prize">Miguel de Cervantes Prize</a>, considered the most important accolade in Spanish-language literature and awarded to authors whose "work has contributed to enrich, in a notable way, the literary patrimony of the Spanish language".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In 2002, Vargas was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/PEN/Nabokov_Award" title="PEN/Nabokov Award">PEN/Nabokov Award</a>. Vargas Llosa also received the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Irving_Kristol_Award" title="Irving Kristol Award">Irving Kristol Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/American_Enterprise_Institute" title="American Enterprise Institute">American Enterprise Institute</a> and was the 2008 recipient of the Harold and Ethel L. Stellfox Visiting Scholar and Writers Award at <a href="/wiki/Dickinson_College" title="Dickinson College">Dickinson College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of Vargas Llosa's works have been adapted for the screen, including <i>The Time of the Hero</i> and <i>Captain Pantoja and the Special Service</i> (both by the Peruvian director <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Lombardi" title="Francisco Lombardi">Francisco Lombardi</a>) and <i>The Feast of the Goat</i> (by Vargas Llosa's cousin, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Llosa" title="Luis Llosa">Luis Llosa</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Aunt_Julia_and_the_Scriptwriter" title="Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter">Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter</a></i> was turned into the English-language film, <i><a href="/wiki/Tune_in_Tomorrow" title="Tune in Tomorrow">Tune in Tomorrow</a></i>. <i>The Feast of the Goat</i> has also been adapted as a theatrical play by <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Al%C3%AD_Triana" title="Jorge Alí Triana">Jorge Alí Triana</a>, a Colombian playwright and director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1967 – <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B3mulo_Gallegos_Prize" title="Rómulo Gallegos Prize">Rómulo Gallegos Prize</a></li>
<li>1986 – <a href="/wiki/Grinzane_Cavour_Prize" title="Grinzane Cavour Prize">Grinzane Cavour Prize</a> for Fiction foreign</li>
<li>1986 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias_Award" title="Prince of Asturias Award">Prince of Asturias Award</a> for Literature</li>
<li>1993 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planeta_Prize" title="Planeta Prize">Planeta Prize</a> for <i>Death in the Andes</i>, a thriller starring one of the characters in <i>Who Killed Palomino Molero?</i></li>
<li>1994 – <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize" title="Miguel de Cervantes Prize">Miguel de Cervantes Prize</a>, after taking Spanish citizenship</li>
<li>1996 – <a href="/wiki/Peace_Prize_of_the_German_Book_Trade" title="Peace Prize of the German Book Trade">Peace Prize of the German Book Trade</a></li>
<li>1999 – <a href="/wiki/Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo_International_Prize" title="Menéndez Pelayo International Prize">Menéndez Pelayo International Prize</a></li>
<li>2004 – Independent Foreign Fiction Prize</li>
<li>2004 – Grinzane Cavour Prize</li>
<li>2006 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Moors_Cabot_prize" title="Maria Moors Cabot prize">Maria Moors Cabot prize</a></li>
<li>2010 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a></li>
<li>2010 – International Award Viareggio-Versilia</li>
<li>2011 - <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Literary_Award" title="St. Louis Literary Award">St. Louis Literary Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Louis_University" title="Saint Louis University">Saint Louis University</a> Library Associates<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li>2012 – "10 Most Influential Ibero American Intellectuals" of the year – Foreign Policy magazine <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.fp-es.org/los-10-intelectuales-iberoamericanos-mas-influyentes-2012" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></li>
<li>2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes_International_Prize_for_Literary_Creation_in_the_Spanish_Language" title="Carlos Fuentes International Prize for Literary Creation in the Spanish Language">Carlos Fuentes International Prize for Literary Creation in the Spanish Language</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li>2016 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pedro_Henr%C3%ADquez_Ure%C3%B1a_International_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pedro Henríquez Ureña International Prize (page does not exist)">Pedro Henríquez Ureña International Prize</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Cross with Diamonds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Sun_(Peru)" title="Order of the Sun (Peru)">Order of the Sun</a> (Peru)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_Cross_of_Honour_for_Science_and_Art,_1st_class" title="Austrian Cross of Honour for Science and Art, 1st class">Austrian Cross of Honour for Science and Art, 1st class</a></li>
<li>Chevalier of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a> (France)</li>
<li>Officer of the <a href="/wiki/Ordre_des_Arts_et_des_Lettres" title="Ordre des Arts et des Lettres">Ordre des Arts et des Lettres</a> (France)</li>
<li>Commander of the Ordre des Arts et des Lettres (France)</li>
<li>Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Aztec_Eagle" title="Order of the Aztec Eagle">Order of the Aztec Eagle</a> (Mexico)</li>
<li>Grand Cross with Silver Star of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_Ruben_Dario&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Order of Ruben Dario (page does not exist)">Order of Ruben Dario</a> (Nicaragua)</li>
<li>Grand Cross with Silver Star of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Order of Christopher Columbus">Order of Christopher Columbus</a> (Dominican Republic)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_works">Selected works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Selected works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiction">Fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1959 – <i>Los jefes</i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Cubs_and_Other_Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Cubs and Other Stories (page does not exist)">The Cubs and Other Stories</a></i>, 1979)</li>
<li>1963 – <i>La ciudad y los perros</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Time_of_the_Hero" title="The Time of the Hero">The Time of the Hero</a></i>, 1966)</li>
<li>1966 – <i>La casa verde</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_House" title="The Green House">The Green House</a></i>, 1968)</li>
<li>1969 – <i>Conversación en la catedral</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Conversation_in_the_Cathedral" title="Conversation in the Cathedral">Conversation in the Cathedral</a></i>, 1975)</li>
<li>1973 – <i>Pantaleón y las visitadoras</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Pantoja_and_the_Special_Service" title="Captain Pantoja and the Special Service">Captain Pantoja and the Special Service</a></i>, 1978)</li>
<li>1977 – <i>La tía Julia y el escribidor</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Aunt_Julia_and_the_Scriptwriter" title="Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter">Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter</a></i>, 1982)</li>
<li>1981 – <i>La guerra del fin del mundo</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_War_of_the_End_of_the_World" title="The War of the End of the World">The War of the End of the World</a></i>, 1984)</li>
<li>1984 – <i>Historia de Mayta</i> (<i>The Real Life of Alejandro Mayta</i>, 1985)</li>
<li>1986 – <i>¿Quién mató a Palomino Molero?</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_Palomino_Molero%3F" title="Who Killed Palomino Molero?">Who Killed Palomino Molero?</a></i>, 1987)</li>
<li>1987 – <i>El hablador</i> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Storyteller_(novel)" title="The Storyteller (novel)">The Storyteller</a></i>, 1989)</li>
<li>1988 – <i>Elogio de la madrastra</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/In_Praise_of_the_Stepmother" title="In Praise of the Stepmother">In Praise of the Stepmother</a></i>, 1990)</li>
<li>1993 – <i>Lituma en los Andes</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_the_Andes" title="Death in the Andes">Death in the Andes</a></i>, 1996)</li>
<li>1997 – <i>Los cuadernos de don Rigoberto</i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Notebooks_of_Don_Rigoberto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Notebooks of Don Rigoberto (page does not exist)">The Notebooks of Don Rigoberto</a></i>, 1998)</li>
<li>2000 – <i>La fiesta del chivo</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Feast_of_the_Goat" title="The Feast of the Goat">The Feast of the Goat</a></i>, 2001)</li>
<li>2003 – <i>El paraíso en la otra esquina</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Way_to_Paradise" title="The Way to Paradise">The Way to Paradise</a></i>, 2003)</li>
<li>2006 – <i>Travesuras de la niña mala</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Bad_Girl" title="The Bad Girl">The Bad Girl</a></i>, 2007)</li>
<li>2010 – <i>El sueño del celta</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Dream_of_the_Celt" title="The Dream of the Celt">The Dream of the Celt</a></i>, 2010)</li>
<li>2013 – <i>El héroe discreto</i> (<i>The Discreet Hero</i>, 2015)</li>
<li>2016 - <i>Cinco esquinas</i> (<i>Five Corners</i>, 2016)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-fiction">Non-fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Non-fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1958 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bases_para_una_interpretaci%C3%B3n_de_Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bases para una interpretación de Rubén Darío (page does not exist)">Bases para una interpretación de Rubén Darío</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_basis_for_interpretation_of_Ruben_Dario&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The basis for interpretation of Ruben Dario (page does not exist)">The basis for interpretation of Ruben Dario</a></i>)</li>
<li>1971 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez:_historia_de_un_deicidio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="García Márquez: historia de un deicidio (page does not exist)">García Márquez: historia de un deicidio</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez:_Story_of_a_Deicide&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="García Márquez: Story of a Deicide (page does not exist)">García Márquez: Story of a Deicide</a></i>)</li>
<li>1975 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_org%C3%ADa_perpetua:_Flaubert_y_%22Madame_Bovary%22&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title='La orgía perpetua: Flaubert y "Madame Bovary" (page does not exist)'>La orgía perpetua: Flaubert y "Madame Bovary"</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Perpetual_Orgy" title="The Perpetual Orgy">The Perpetual Orgy</a></i>)</li>
<li>1990 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_verdad_de_las_mentiras:_ensayos_sobre_la_novela_moderna&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La verdad de las mentiras: ensayos sobre la novela moderna (page does not exist)">La verdad de las mentiras: ensayos sobre la novela moderna</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=A_Writer%27s_Reality&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="A Writer's Reality (page does not exist)">A Writer's Reality</a></i>)</li>
<li>1993 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_pez_en_el_agua._Memorias&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El pez en el agua. Memorias (page does not exist)">El pez en el agua. Memorias</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/A_Fish_in_the_Water" title="A Fish in the Water">A Fish in the Water</a></i>)</li>
<li>1995 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hitos_y_Mitos_Literarios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hitos y Mitos Literarios (page does not exist)">Hitos y Mitos Literarios</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Milestones_and_the_Stories_of_Greatest_Literary_Works&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Milestones and the Stories of Greatest Literary Works (page does not exist)">The Milestones and the Stories of Greatest Literary Works</a></i>) (Illustrations by <a href="/wiki/Willi_Glasauer" title="Willi Glasauer">Willi Glasauer</a>), (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%ADrculo_de_Lectores&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Círculo de Lectores (page does not exist)">Círculo de Lectores</a>)</li>
<li>1996 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_utop%C3%ADa_arcaica:_Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Arguedas_y_las_ficciones_del_indigenismo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La utopía arcaica: José María Arguedas y las ficciones del indigenismo (page does not exist)">La utopía arcaica: José María Arguedas y las ficciones del indigenismo</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Archaic_utopia:_Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Arguedas_and_the_fictions_of_indigenismo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Archaic utopia: José María Arguedas and the fictions of indigenismo (page does not exist)">Archaic utopia: José María Arguedas and the fictions of indigenismo</a></i>)</li>
<li>1997 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cartas_a_un_joven_novelista&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cartas a un joven novelista (page does not exist)">Cartas a un joven novelista</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Letters_to_a_Young_Novelist&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Letters to a Young Novelist (page does not exist)">Letters to a Young Novelist</a></i>)</li>
<li>2000 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nationalismus_als_neue_Bedrohung&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nationalismus als neue Bedrohung (page does not exist)">Nationalismus als neue Bedrohung</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nationalism_as_a_new_threat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nationalism as a new threat (page does not exist)">Nationalism as a new threat</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kordi_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kordi-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>2001 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_lenguaje_de_la_pasi%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El lenguaje de la pasión (page does not exist)">El lenguaje de la pasión</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Language_of_Passion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Language of Passion (page does not exist)">The Language of Passion</a></i>)</li>
<li>2004 – <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_tentaci%C3%B3n_de_lo_imposible" title="La tentación de lo imposible">La tentación de lo imposible</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Temptation_of_the_Impossible" title="The Temptation of the Impossible">The Temptation of the Impossible</a></i>)</li>
<li>2007 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Preg%C3%B3n_de_Sevilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Pregón de Sevilla (page does not exist)">El Pregón de Sevilla</a></i> (as <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Introduction_for_LOS_TOROS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Introduction for LOS TOROS (page does not exist)">Introduction for LOS TOROS</a></i>)</li>
<li>2009 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_viaje_a_la_ficci%C3%B3n:_El_mundo_de_Juan_Carlos_Onetti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El viaje a la ficción: El mundo de Juan Carlos Onetti (page does not exist)">El viaje a la ficción: El mundo de Juan Carlos Onetti</a></i></li>
<li>2011 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Touchstones:_Essays_on_Literature,_Art,_and_Politics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Touchstones: Essays on Literature, Art, and Politics (page does not exist)">Touchstones: Essays on Literature, Art, and Politics</a></i></li>
<li>2012 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_civilizaci%C3%B3n_del_espect%C3%A1culo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La civilización del espectáculo (page does not exist)">La civilización del espectáculo</a></i></li>
<li>2012 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=In_Praise_of_Reading_and_Fiction:_The_Nobel_Lecture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="In Praise of Reading and Fiction: The Nobel Lecture (page does not exist)">In Praise of Reading and Fiction: The Nobel Lecture</a></i></li>
<li>2014 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mi_trayectora_intelectual&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mi trayectora intelectual (page does not exist)">Mi trayectora intelectual</a></i> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=My_Intellectual_Journey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="My Intellectual Journey (page does not exist)">My Intellectual Journey</a></i>)</li>
<li>2015 – <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Notes_on_the_Death_of_Culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Notes on the Death of Culture (page does not exist)">Notes on the Death of Culture</a></i></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drama">Drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mario_Vargas_Llosa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Drama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1952 – <i>La huida del inca</i></li>
<li>1981 – <i>La señorita de Tacna</i></li>
<li>1983 – <i>Kathie y el hipopótamo</i></li>
<li>1986 – <i>La Chunga</i></li>
<li>1993 – <i>El loco de los balcones</i></li>
<li>1996 – <i>Ojos bonitos, cuadros feos</i></li>
<li>2007 – <i>Odiseo y Penélope</i></li>
<li>2008 – <i>Al pie del Támesis</i></li>
<li>2010 – <i>Las mil y una noches</i></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>Vargas Llosa's essays and journalism have been collected as <i>Contra viento y marea</i>, issued in three volumes (1983, 1986, and 1990). A selection has been edited by John King and translated and published as <i>Making Waves</i>. 2003 – "The Language of Passion"</p>

<tr>
<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Novels</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Time_of_the_Hero" title="The Time of the Hero">The Time of the Hero</a></i> (1963)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_House" title="The Green House">The Green House</a></i> (1966)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Conversation_in_the_Cathedral" title="Conversation in the Cathedral">Conversation in the Cathedral</a></i> (1969)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Pantoja_and_the_Special_Service" title="Captain Pantoja and the Special Service">Captain Pantoja and the Special Service</a></i> (1973)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Aunt_Julia_and_the_Scriptwriter" title="Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter">Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter</a></i> (1977)</li>
